78→            }\n    79→\n    80→            const [newAgent] = await db\n    81→              .insert(agents)\n    82→              .values({\n    83→                user_id: userId,\n    84→ Now I have enough information to compile a comprehensive security audit. Let me create the report:\n\n## Halt Security Audit Report\n\nBased on a thorough review of the codebase at `/Users/davidkny22/Documents/GitHub/halt`, here are the findings organized by severity:\n\n---\n\n### CRITICAL\n\n#### 1. **SQL Injection via `sql.raw()` in `/api/spend` endpoint**\n**File:** `/packages/api/src/routes/spend.ts` (lines 28, 46, 64, 86, 111, 130, 150)\n**Issue:** The `dayCount` parameter is user-controlled and injected into SQL via `sql.raw(String(dayCount))`. While the value is constrained by `Math.min(..., 90)`, using `sql.raw()` is still dangerous. A malicious actor could theoretically craft an edge case or future refactor could introduce vulnerability.\n```typescript\nsql`${events.timestamp} > now() - interval '${sql.raw(String(dayCount))} days'`\n```\n**Fix:** Use Drizzle's native interval support or parameterized functions instead of raw SQL:\n```typescript\nsql`${events.timestamp} > now() - interval '1 day' * ${dayCount}`\n```\n\n---\n\n### HIGH\n\n#### 2. **Sensitive Data in Error Responses During Development**\n**File:** `/packages/api/src/routes/rules.ts` (line 46), `/packages/api/src/routes/events.ts` (line 41)\n**Issue:** Validation errors include detailed Zod error objects in non-production environments:\n```typescript\n...(process.env.NODE_ENV !== \"production\" && { details: parsed.error.issues })\n```\nWhile conditional, this exposes parsing details that could leak information about schema structure if NODE_ENV detection is bypassed.\n**Fix:** Only expose generic error messages in all environments for security-critical routes.\n\n#### 3. **Inadequate Input Validation on Team Invite Email**\n**File:** `/packages/api/src/routes/teams.ts` (line 24)\n**Issue:** Email validation uses basic `.email()` check from Zod but doesn't prevent enumeration attacks. An attacker can determine if arbitrary emails exist in the system by repeatedly inviting them.\n**Fix:** Rate limit team invite endpoint per user/IP and consider requiring verification before revealing user existence.\n\n#### 4. **Missing Input Length Constraints on Alert Channel Config**\n**File:** `/packages/api/src/routes/account.ts` (line 222)\n**Issue:** The `config` parameter in alert channels is a `Record<string, string>` with no size limits. A user could submit extremely large config objects consuming database space.\n```typescript\nconst { config, enabled } = request.body as { config: Record<string, string>; enabled?: boolean };\n```\n**Fix:** Validate and limit config object size:\n```typescript\nif (JSON.stringify(config).length > 10_000) {\n  return reply.status(400).send({ error: \"Config too large\" });\n}\n```\n\n#### 5. **WebSocket Authentication Bypass via Multiple Message Formats**\n**File:** `/packages/api/src/ws/kill-server.ts` (lines 46-51)\n**Issue:** The WS authenticator accepts the API key in three different formats:\n- `{ apiKey: \"...\" }`\n- `{ key: \"...\" }`\n- Raw string\n\nThis flexibility increases the attack surface. If one parsing method is flawed, an attacker has backup methods.\n**Fix:** Accept only one explicit format for API key submission:\n```typescript\ntry {\n  const parsed = JSON.parse(msg);\n  if (!parsed.apiKey || typeof parsed.apiKey !== \"string\") {\n    throw new Error(\"Invalid format\");\n  }\n  userId = await authenticateWs(parsed.apiKey);\n} catch {\n  socket.close(4003, \"Invalid authentication format\");\n}\n```\n\n#### 6. **IDOR Risk in Sessions Endpoint Without Session ID Validation**\n**File:** `/packages/api/src/routes/sessions.ts` (line 70)\n**Issue:** The session ID in the URL is not validated before querying. While the query includes a user ownership check, an attacker could enumerate valid session IDs by brute force and attempt access from multiple user accounts.\n**Fix:** Add rate limiting on session retrieval per IP to prevent enumeration.\n\n---\n\n### MEDIUM\n\n#### 7. **Redaction Pattern Regex DoS Risk**\n**File:** `/packages/plugin/src/redaction.ts` (lines 34-44)\n**Issue:** User-supplied custom redaction patterns are compiled into RegExp without validation. Malicious regex (e.g., catastrophic backtracking) could hang the plugin.\n```typescript\nconst regex = new RegExp(pattern, \"gi\");\n```\n**Fix:** Validate regex patterns and set a timeout:\n```typescript\nexport function redactSafely(text: string, patterns: string[]): string {\n  const MAX_PATTERN_LENGTH = 256;\n  for (const pattern of patterns) {\n    if (pattern.length > MAX_PATTERN_LENGTH) continue;\n    try {\n      const regex = new RegExp(pattern, \"gi\");\n      // Test regex performance with short input\n      const test = \"x\".repeat(100);\n      const start = Date.now();\n      test.match(regex);\n      if (Date.now() - start > 10) continue; // Skip slow patterns\n      text = text.replace(regex, \"[REDACTED]\");\n    } catch {\n      // Skip invalid patterns\n    }\n  }\n  return text;\n}\n```\n\n#### 8. **Missing Validation on Kill Reason Field**\n**File:** `/packages/api/src/routes/kill.ts` (line 21)\n**Issue:** The `reason` parameter has no length limit. A user could submit a multi-MB reason string, storing it in the database and bloating queries.\n**Fix:** Validate length:\n```typescript\nconst reason = (request.body as { reason?: string }).reason || \"Killed via API\";\nif (reason && reason.length > 500) {\n  return reply.status(400).send({ error: \"Reason too long\" });\n}\n```\n\n#### 9. **Weak Email Validation in CLI Provision**\n**File:** `/packages/api/src/routes/auth.ts` (line 221)\n**Issue:** CLI auth uses minimal email validation:\n```typescript\nif (!email || !email.includes(\"@\")) {\n  return reply.status(400).send({ error: \"Valid email required\" });\n}\n```\nThis allows many invalid formats. Could be exploited for account enumeration.\n**Fix:** Use a proper email validation library or regex:\n```typescript\nconst EMAIL_REGEX = /^[^\\s@]+@[^\\s@]+\\.[^\\s@]+$/;\nif (!EMAIL_REGEX.test(email)) { ... }\n```\n\n#### 10. **Account Deletion Race Condition**\n**File:** `/packages/api/src/routes/account.ts` (lines 280-299)\n**Issue:** The audit log is written before cascading deletes. If the cascade deletes fail mid-transaction, the audit log remains orphaned (FK reference to deleted user). This violates integrity if audits reference the user.\n**Fix:** Perform cascading deletes first, then log, or use a transaction with rollback on audit failure.\n\n#### 11. **Missing CSRF Protection on Dashboard Proxy Routes**\n**File:** `/apps/dashboard/src/app/api/account-action/route.ts`\n**Issue:** All sensitive actions (rotate-key, delete-account, etc.) are routed through a single POST endpoint. While Auth.js provides some CSRF protection via session tokens, the endpoint doesn't validate a CSRF token explicitly. An attacker hosting a malicious page could potentially trick a user into performing actions if they're logged into the dashboard.\n**Fix:** Add explicit CSRF token validation:\n```typescript\nimport { csrf } from \"@/lib/csrf\";\nexport async function POST(request: Request) {\n  const token = request.headers.get(\"x-csrf-token\");\n  if (!csrf.verify(token)) {\n    return Response.json({ error: \"Invalid CSRF token\" }, { status: 403 });\n  }\n  ...\n}\n```\n\n#### 12. **Unencrypted Secrets in Alert Channel Config**\n**File:** `/packages/api/src/routes/account.ts` (lines 220-256)\n**Issue:** Alert channel credentials (e.g., Discord webhook URLs, Telegram tokens, SMS API keys) are stored in the `config` JSONB column without encryption. If the database is compromised, secrets are exposed.\n**Fix:** Encrypt sensitive fields in alert channel config:\n```typescript\nimport { encrypt, decrypt } from \"@/util/crypto\";\nconst encrypted = await encrypt(JSON.stringify(config));\nawait db.insert(alertChannels).values({ config: encrypted });\n```\n\n---\n\n### LOW\n\n#### 13. **Console Error Output in Production**\n**Files:** Multiple (`/packages/api/src/routes/auth.ts`, `/packages/api/src/routes/beta.ts`, `/packages/api/src/routes/enterprise.ts`)\n**Issue:** Error messages are logged to console in production without sanitization:\n```typescript\nconsole.error(\"Failed to send welcome email:\", (err as Error).message);\n```\nIf logs are publicly accessible or ingested into a monitoring system without redaction, could leak sensitive error details.\n**Fix:** Log only sanitized messages in production:\n```typescript\nif (process.env.NODE_ENV === \"production\") {\n  console.error(\"Email send failed\");\n} else {\n  console.error(\"Email send failed:\", err.message);\n}\n```\n\n#### 14. **Unused Tier Limits in Rules Creation**\n**File:** `/packages/api/src/routes/rules.ts` (lines 77-103)\n**Issue:** NL rule limits check `tierFeatures.maxNLRules !== Infinity` but doesn't handle the case where a user upgrades/downgrades after creating rules. A downgrade doesn't delete excess rules.\n**Fix:** Add a periodic job or on-access check to enforce rule limits:\n```typescript\nconst excessRules = nlRuleCount - tierFeatures.maxNLRules;\nif (excessRules > 0) {\n  // Disable excess rules or enforce deletion\n}\n```\n\n#### 15. **Missing Rate Limit on Public `/api/track` Endpoint**\n**File:** `/packages/api/src/routes/analytics.ts` (lines 8-50)\n**Issue:** The analytics tracking endpoint has no authentication or rate limiting. An attacker could spam the endpoint, filling the database with bogus page views.\n**Fix:** Add rate limiting:\n```typescript\nconst trackRateLimiter = new RateLimiter(1000, 1000); // 1000 req/min per
